## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by time t and current population size P, which is the standard setup for single-species population dynamics modeled by ordinary differential equations with density dependence, time-varying forcing, and harvesting/mortality terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Per-capita growth decomposition: dP_dt = P * g(P, t) (modeling growth rate via per-capita rate)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear density dependence: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P) (per-capita rate decreases/increases linearly with P)
- Logistic ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity limitation with K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (nonlinear density dependence; c2 controls curvature)
- Richards-type generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) ** c3 (extra shape flexibility for approach to capacity)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic density dependence; asymmetric approach to capacity)
- Allee effect (strong Allee): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (negative growth at low P; c2 ≈ 1/A)
- Allee effect (weak/offset): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P + c3) (low-density modification without mandatory negative growth)
- Constant harvesting/stocking: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (external removals/additions independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P (net per-capita reduction/addition term)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (1 + c3 * P) (effort-limited removal that saturates with P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (changing resources/habitat over time)
- Pulse/episodic effects (smooth approximation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * exp(-c3 * (t - c4) ** 2) (temporary shocks such as migration/management)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Compute per-capita rate first: model g(P,t) = dP_dt / P to distinguish density-independent vs density-dependent mechanisms (g constant vs g decreasing with P).
- Carrying-capacity limitation often appears as a negative feedback factor multiplying P, e.g., (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)^nu), giving a single stable equilibrium at P ≈ 1/c.
- Gompertz-type dynamics are suggested when per-capita growth decreases approximately with log(P), yielding dP_dt proportional to P*log(K/P) and an asymmetric approach to K.
- Allee effects are indicated when dP_dt becomes negative at low P; structurally this requires an additional low-P factor such as (c*P - 1) multiplying the usual P term.
- Harvesting or immigration typically enters additively (±c0, ±c0*P, or saturating ±c0*P/(1+c1*P)), which can shift equilibria or create extinction thresholds.
- Seasonality/forcing is often captured by making the per-capita term periodic in t (sin/cos), producing oscillatory deviations around the unforced equilibrium.
- If growth slows over time independent of P (e.g., aging habitat), allow parameters like carrying capacity or intrinsic rate to be simple functions of t (linear, exponential, or periodic).
- Multiple equilibria/bistability in single-species models generally requires non-monotone per-capita growth in P, often implemented via higher-order products like P*(1-c1*P)*(c2*P-1).

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG7)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P**c9
Candidate formulas: 55

Let \(P\) be the only effective variable in the GT (since GT has no \(t\)-dependence). First rewrite the GT into a simple polynomial-in-\(P\) plus \(P^{1/3}\) form.

### Ground Truth simplification
GT:
\[
0.721355\;(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P \;+\; 0.721355\;(1-P/b)P \;+\; 0.721355\;P^{1/3}
\]
with \(a=6.6511035\), \(b=13.5380926\).

Expand the first two terms:

- \((-1+P/a)P = -P + P^2/a\)
- Multiply by \((1-P/b)\):
\[
(-P + P^2/a)(1-P/b)=(-P + P^2/a) - (-P + P^2/a)\,P/b
\]
\[
= -P + P^2/a + P^2/b - P^3/(ab)
\]
- Second term: \((1-P/b)P = P - P^2/b\)

Add them: the \(-P\) and \(+P\) cancel, and \(+P^2/b\) cancels \(-P^2/b\), leaving:
\[
P^2/a - P^3/(ab)
\]

So GT is exactly:
\[
0.721355\left(\frac{1}{a}P^2 - \frac{1}{ab}P^3 + P^{1/3}\right)
\]
i.e. of the form
\[
\alpha P^{1/3} + \beta P^2 + \gamma P^3
\]
with fixed nonzero \(\alpha,\beta,\gamma\), and **no other terms** and **no \(t\)**.

Therefore, any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by choosing its constants) to exactly \(\alpha P^{1/3}+\beta P^2+\gamma P^3\), with no extra \(P\), constants, logs, trig, exp, abs, or \(t\)-dependence.

---

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3 P^2 + c4\sin(c5+c6 t)\)
Set \(c4=0\) to remove the \(t\)-dependent sine. Then it becomes \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^3+(c2+c3)P^2\), which can match GT by choosing \(c0=\alpha\), \(c1=\gamma\), \(c2+c3=\beta\). **Matches.**

### 2. Adds \(P c4\) and \(P c5\cos(c6 t+c7)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence set \(c5=0\). Still has a \(P c4\) term; GT has no linear \(P\) term, so set \(c4=0\). Remaining is \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^3+(c2+c3)P^2\). **Matches.**

### 3. Has \(c4\log(Pc5+1)\cos(c6 t)\)
To eliminate \(t\), either force \(\cos(c6 t)\) constant by \(c6=0\) (gives \(\cos 0=1\)) but then you still have a \(\log(Pc5+1)\) term which GT doesn’t have for all \(P\). Only way is \(c4=0\). Then reduces to the needed monomials. **Matches.**

### 4. Has \(c5 P^{c4}\cos(c6 t+c7)\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c6=0\) so cosine is constant \(\cos(c7)\). Then term is constant\(\times P^{c4}\). GT has only exponents \(1/3,2,3\). You could set this extra term to 0 by \(c5=0\) (or \(\cos(c7)=0\)). Then reduces to required monomials. **Matches.**

### 5. Has \(c4 e^{Pc5}\)
Exponential in \(P\) cannot equal a polynomial+fractional power for all \(P\) unless removed: set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 6. Has \(c4\sin(Pc5+c6)\)
Sine in \(P\) must be removed: set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 7. Has \(P c4 (P c5)^{c6} + P c7\)
This introduces a linear \(P\) term unless \(c7=0\). The other added term is \(c4 c5^{c6} P^{c6+1}\), a monomial. To avoid introducing an exponent other than \(2\) or \(3\), either set \(c4=0\) or choose \(c6+1\in\{2,3\}\). Easiest: set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 8. Has \(P c3 + P c4 + P c5(1-(Pc6)^{c7})^{c8}\)
GT has no linear \(P\), so need \(c3=c4=0\). The last term is generally non-polynomial; to remove it set \(c5=0\). Then left with \(c0P^3+(c1+c2)P^2\) but **no \(P^{1/3}\)** term, so cannot match GT (GT has nonzero \(P^{1/3}\)). **No match.**

### 9. Has \(c4\log(c5 e^{Pc6}+1)\)
Non-algebraic in \(P\); must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 10. Has \(P c4(1-(Pc5)^{c6})^{c7}\)
Non-polynomial generally; must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 11. Has extra \(c5 P^{c4}\)
If kept, exponent must be one of \(\{1/3,2,3\}\) and coefficient must merge correctly; but we already have all needed monomials, so simplest set \(c5=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 12. Has \(c5 P^{c4}\log(Pc6+1)\)
Log term must be removed: set \(c5=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 13. Has rational terms \(P c4/(Pc5+c6)+c7/(Pc5+c6)\)
These are not polynomial unless removed. Setting \(c4=c7=0\) removes them. Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 14. No \(P^{1/3}\) term at all
Even if log term removed, expression is only \(P^3,P^2,P\). Cannot create \(P^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 15. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 16. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 17. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 18. Has \(P c4 + c5\)
GT has no constant or linear term; set \(c4=0,c5=0\). Remaining matches monomials. **Matches.**

### 19. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 20. Has \(P c4\log(c5/|P|+1)\)
Non-algebraic and also involves \(|P|\); must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 21. Has \(c5 P^{c4} e^{c6 t}\)
To remove \(t\), either \(c5=0\) or \(c6=0\) (making \(e^{0}=1\)). If \(c6=0\), term becomes \(c5 P^{c4}\) which could be absorbed, but easiest set \(c5=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 22. Has \(P c4/(Pc5+1)\)
Rational in \(P\) unless removed: set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 23. Has \(c4\cos(c5\log(c6|P|+1))\)
Non-algebraic in \(P\); must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 24. Has \(P c7\) and multiple \(P^2,P^3\) terms
Set \(c7=0\) to remove linear term. Then you can combine \(P^3\) coefficients \((c1+c2)\) and \(P^2\) coefficients \((c3+c4+c5+c6)\). Also has \(P^{1/3}c0\). So can match. **Matches.**

### 25. Has \(P c5\)
Set \(c5=0\). Remaining has \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **Matches.**

### 26. Has \(c4\log(Pc5+1)\)
Must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 27. Only \(P^{1/3},P^3,P^2,P\)
Has a linear \(P c3\); set \(c3=0\). Then matches. **Matches.**

### 28. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 29. Has \(P c4 (c5+t)^{c6}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, need \(c4=0\) (since \((c5+t)^{c6}\) cannot be constant for all \(t\) unless degenerate in ways that still don’t hold for all \(t\)). With \(c4=0\), reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 30. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 31. Has constant \(c3\)
GT has no constant term; set \(c3=0\). Then matches. **Matches.**

### 32. Has constant \(c4\)
Set \(c4=0\). Then matches. **Matches.**

### 33. Exactly \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^3+(c2+c3)P^2\)
Directly matches by choosing constants. **Matches.**

### 34. Uses \(|P|^{1/3}\) not \(P^{1/3}\)
Even if coefficients chosen, \(|P|^{1/3}\neq P^{1/3}\) for negative \(P\). Since equivalence must hold for all real \(P\), cannot match GT’s \(P^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 35. Only adds another \(P^2\) term
Combine \(P^2\) coefficients; matches. **Matches.**

### 36. Lacks a \(P^2\) *and* \(P^3\) simultaneously? Actually has \(P^{1/3},P^3,P^2\) yes.
It is \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^3+c2P^2\). Matches. **Matches.**

### 37. Has fixed \(+P^2\) term (coefficient 1)
Still fine: total \(P^2\) coefficient is \(c2+1\), can set \(c2=\beta-1\). Matches. **Matches.**

### 38. No linear term, has \(P^{1/3}\), multiple \(P^2,P^3\)
Combine coefficients to match. **Matches.**

### 39. Has \(c4 e^{c5 t}\log(c6|P|+1)\)
To match GT (no \(t\), no log), must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 40. Has \(P^2 c2/(c3 t+1)\) and linear \(P c6\)
To remove \(t\), need \(c2=0\) or \(c3=0\). Also must remove linear term: \(c6=0\). If \(c2=0\), you still have \(P^{1/3},P^3,P^2\) via \(c4,c5\). So can match. **Matches.**

### 41. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 42. No \(P^{1/3}\) term
Cannot match. **No match.**

### 43. Has \(P c4 e^{c5 t}\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c4=0\) (or \(c5=0\) gives linear \(P\) still). With \(c4=0\), reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 44. Has \(t\)-rational terms
Must remove them: set \(c4=c7=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 45. Has \(t\) in numerator over \(Pc5+c6\)
To remove \(t\) dependence, must set \(c4=0\). Also rational term \(c7/(Pc5+c6)\) must be removed: set \(c7=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 46. Has \(c4 t + c5\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c4=0\). To remove constant, set \(c5=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 47. Has \(P c4/(c5 t+c6)+c7/(c5 t+c6)\)
To remove \(t\), must set \(c4=c7=0\) (otherwise depends on \(t\)). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 48. Has \(c4 e^{c5 t}\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 49. Has \(c4 t (P+c5)^{c6}\)
Contains factor \(t\); to remove \(t\) must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 50. Has \(c4\log(c5 t+1)\)
To remove \(t\), must set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 51. Has complicated \(\log(\cdots + c8 e^{c9 t^2}+1)\)
To remove \(t\) and log, set \(c4=0\). Then reduces properly. **Matches.**

### 52. Has \(\log(c5 e^{Pc6+c7 t}+1)\)

I need to first simplify the Ground Truth expression to understand its structure.

**GT expression:**
```
0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P^(1/3)
```

Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511035054181695`, `d = 13.538092585698905`.

**First term:** `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
**Second term:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P`
**Third term:** `a*P^(1/3)`

Let me combine the first two terms. Factor out `a*(1 - P/d)*P`:
```
a*(1 - P/d)*P * [(-1 + P/b) + 1] = a*(1 - P/d)*P * (P/b)
= a*P²/b * (1 - P/d)
= a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)
```

So GT = `a*P^(1/3) + (a/b)*P² - (a/(b*d))*P³`

Computing constants:
- `a/b = 0.7213553457664288 / 6.6511035054181695 ≈ 0.10845`
- `a/(b*d) = 0.10845 / 13.538092585698905 ≈ 0.008012`

So **GT = a*P^(1/3) + α*P² + β*P³** where α ≈ 0.10845 and β ≈ -0.008012.

This is simply: **GT = c*P^(1/3) + c'*P² + c''*P³**

Now I check each candidate for the form `A*P^(1/3) + B*P² + C*P³` (with no dependence on `t` and no other basis functions).
